Title: Extremely Inefficient Star Formation in the Outer Disks of 
       Nearby Galaxies 
Authors: Bigiel F., Leroy A., Walter F., Blitz L., Brinks E., de Blok W.J.G., 
         Madore B. 
Table: Data for individual sampling points from the optical disks (r<r25)
================================================================================
Byte-by-byte Description of file: aj351668t2_mrt.txt
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   Bytes Format Units               Label   Explanations
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   1- 12 A12    ---                 Sample  Galaxy sample (1)
  14- 24 A11    ---                 Name    Galaxy name (2)
  26- 29 F4.2   [solMass/pc2]       logHI   ? Log H I surface density (3)
  31- 34 F4.2   [solMass/pc2]     e_logHI   Uncertainty in logHI (4)
  36- 39 F4.2   [solMass/pc2]       logH2   ? Log H2 surface density (3)
  41- 44 F4.2   [solMass/pc2]     e_logH2   ? Uncertainty in logH2 (4)
  46- 50 F5.2   [solMass/yr/kpc2]   logSFR  ? Log SFR surface density (3)
  52- 56 F5.2   [solMass/yr/kpc2]   elogSFR Uncertainty in logSFR (4)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Note (1):
  HI-dominated = the sample of HI-dominated galaxies from Bigiel et al. (2008).
       Spirals = the sample of spiral galaxies with H2-dominated centers 
                 from Bigiel et al. (2008).
Note (2): References: 
          Sampling points and this result: Bigiel et al. (2008).
          HI Maps: THINGS, Walter et al. (2008).
          Galaxy Distance and Orientation: Walter et al. (2008).
          SFR Maps: SINGS IR (Kennicutt et al. 2003), GALEX FUV
            (Gil de Paz et al. 2007), combination (Leroy et al. 2008)
          CO Maps: HERACLES (Leroy et al. 2009), BIMA SONG (only NGC 5194,
            Helfer et al . 2003).
Note (3): Contrary to the paper, HI and H2 surface densities include a factor
          of 1.36 to account for helium. The data were sampled at a common
          physical resolution of 750pc. Surface densities are corrected to
          account for inclination. Assumptions to convert CO to H2:
          XCO = 2e20 cm^-2^/(K km/s), I(2-1)/I(1-0) = 0.8. Star formation
          rate is traced by UV and IR emission. Calibration assumes a
          Kroupa IMF. Data points are roughly independent, but slight
          oversampling does occur in some regions.
Note (4): HI sensitivity ~ 1 Msun/pc2, calibration uncertainty ~10%. 
          H2 sensitivity (only in spiral sample) ~ 4 Msun/pc2 (HERACLES) 
          or ~13 Msun/pc2 (BIMA SONG), calibration uncertainty ~25%, XCO
          uncertainty not included but we suggest 50%.
          SFR sensitivity ~ 2e-4 Msun/yr/kpc^2, calibration uncertainty ~50% 
          but covariant within a galaxy (from comparison with other tracers). 
          Where there is no data (NaN) or the measurement is not significant, 
          the respective column contains no entry and the uncertainty gives 
          the upper limit.  
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
